  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_95a457ba-5af3-4d09-b2c4-256030bcafaf'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

It took about two chapters of, I don't know, recap of past events? introduction of char<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">Not realizing this was book 4, this is the one I started with. It took about two chapters of, I don't know, recap of past events? introduction of characters? before it grabbed me. In fact, I almost returned it. But I'm glad I didn't. By about chapter 3, it was pretty gripping, and now I can hardly put it down.<a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_2315378692" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2315378692" />
    <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus"><img alt="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588320656p2/78485297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2315378692?book_show_action=true">Mar 03, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) " href="/user/show/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus">Mario the lone bookwolf (semi reviewing hiatus ) </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/78485297-mario-the-lone-bookwolf-semi-reviewing-hiatus?shelf=butcher-jim">butcher-jim</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2315378692" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8810831517208486867">I had to think of Sandersons´ Laws of magic while reading the novels because there are more and more differences between oldfashioned worlds that use the inner character personalization universe as a contrast point in mixture with the world and the fantasy and the new works that unite all elements.<br/><a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_and_soft_magic_systems#Sanderson's_laws_of_magic'>https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_an...</a><br/><br/>And I would subjectively say that the amalgamation of every aspect of the story in the character makes the works more complex and opens plot options that wouldn´</span>
  <span id="freeText8810831517208486867" style="display:none">I had to think of Sandersons´ Laws of magic while reading the novels because there are more and more differences between oldfashioned worlds that use the inner character personalization universe as a contrast point in mixture with the world and the fantasy and the new works that unite all elements.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_and_soft_magic_systems#Sanderson&#39;s_laws_of_magic">https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hard_an...</a><br /><br />And I would subjectively say that the amalgamation of every aspect of the story in the character makes the works more complex and opens plot options that wouldn´t be possible if the intrinsic motivation of the protagonists isn´t directly linked to their abilities, superpowers, sheer will,...<br /><br />This is of cause a huge matter and question of taste too, as some might like their magic info dumping separated from their beloved characters and their development curve and hero´s journey, but for the readers who like the more and more dominating quick, fast cut, cliffhangery, newer writing style, many of the new fantasy authors, who often do great characterization too, may be the revelation.<br /><br />I do like the Canim, it may be possible that mammals evolve to higher intelligence, but don´t lose their instincts, scent, hierarchies, archaic warrior castes,… and it´s an interesting topic in Sci-Fi and fantasy, but a bit underrepresented in fantasy. The evil may be pure evil or something between or not evil in the real sense, just forced to do it, but a whole evolution of complex species is often more something for the main protagonists or their allies, not the standard orcs and evil minions.<br /><br />In sci-fi, on the other hand, it´s logical that with the advanced technological development each fraction that is relevant to the plot has to have a certain military strength and the endless source for new ideas is creating fresh and tasty combinations of the level of how society, mentality, and tech cooperate.<br /><br />Tropes show how literature is conceptualized and created and which mixture of elements makes works and genres unique: <br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Creator/JimButcher">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.php/Literature/CodexAlera">https://tvtropes.org/pmwiki/pmwiki.ph...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="8810831517208486867" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2143842126" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2143842126" />
    <a title="Anne" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1720620-anne"><img alt="Anne" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1415374035p2/1720620.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2143842126?book_show_action=true">Oct 11, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anne" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anne" href="/user/show/1720620-anne">Anne</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7089452-captain-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1720620-anne?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2143842126" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6223944275291042993"><b>My least favorite, so far.</b><br/>I love to read about Tavi and his immediate circle of friends - Kitai, Max, Ehren, Crassus, Marcus. I love to read about what political hijinks Lord & Lady Aquitaine are up to, and what Lady Aria Placida, Issana & Araris are doing to try to help stop them. And I love to read about Fidelias and his struggle to play both sides against each other. <br/>But Bernard and Amara are just as dull as dishwater.<br/>I mean, I <i>like</i> them, but I tend to zone out a tad when reading about their </span>
  <span id="freeText6223944275291042993" style="display:none"><b>My least favorite, so far.</b><br>I love to read about Tavi and his immediate circle of friends - Kitai, Max, Ehren, Crassus, Marcus. I love to read about what political hijinks Lord &amp; Lady Aquitaine are up to, and what Lady Aria Placida, Issana &amp; Araris are doing to try to help stop them. And I love to read about Fidelias and his struggle to play both sides against each other. <br>But Bernard and Amara are just as dull as dishwater.<br>I mean, I <i>like</i> them, but I tend to zone out a tad when reading about their adventures. And this time around they were even more boring than usual.<br><b>Zzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzzz.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507727098ra/24142891.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Too big a chunk of the story was spent following Bernard, Amara, and Gaius on their loooooong journey to Lord Kalare's lands.<br><b>They're heading into the woods!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507727098ra/24142892.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Now it's raining!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507727098ra/24142893.gif" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Now they're in a swamp!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507727098ra/24142894.gif" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br><b>Will they make it in time to save the day?!</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507727098ra/24142895.gif" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, yes. It wasn't like things didn't happen to them on the journey, but none of those things needed to be described in any sort of detail. Butcher could have told us where they were going and why, skipped over all the traveling through the woods crap, and then had them show up and do their thing at the end. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507728015ra/24143020.gif" width="350" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Boom! Done!</b> &lt;-- I would have enjoyed the book a lot more. <br><br>But there were some <i>really</i> cool stories that unfolded in <b>Captain's Fury</b>, and those kept me coming back for more.<br>Gaius leaves Tavi and his legion with some high-ranking political vipers, which leads him into several (seemingly) impossible situations with massive moral and legal ramifications. <br>Of course, I knew Tavi would fix it in some ingenious way.<br>But that confidence was in no small part due to the spoilery, idiotic names of these books.<br>Seriously? Come <i>on</i>, Butcher!<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1507728769ra/24143097.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Still. <br>For all its faults, I'm totally into this series and I can't wait to read the next one!</span>

    <a title="Evgeny" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny"><img alt="Evgeny" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1544797852p2/9340136.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1401822708?book_show_action=true">Sep 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Evgeny" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Evgeny" href="/user/show/9340136-evgeny">Evgeny</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9340136-evgeny?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1401822708" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5295019497458052648">This installment picks up right where the previous one left, so expect some minor spoilers that I will try to minimize. The rebellion of a High Lord still goes on; the invading force is still present in Alera. Tavi and other regulars of the series are still where they were left in the end of book 3. The High Lord of Alera decided that enough is enough and it is time to abandon the diplomacy and show people his raw power. <br/><br/>What is the problem with this? It left Tavi to deal with diplomacy and resu</span>
  <span id="freeText5295019497458052648" style="display:none">This installment picks up right where the previous one left, so expect some minor spoilers that I will try to minimize. The rebellion of a High Lord still goes on; the invading force is still present in Alera. Tavi and other regulars of the series are still where they were left in the end of book 3. The High Lord of Alera decided that enough is enough and it is time to abandon the diplomacy and show people his raw power. <br><br>What is the problem with this? It left Tavi to deal with diplomacy and resulting bureaucracy. This part of the series clearly shows that bureaucracy can be deadlier than invasion of barbarians, alien forces, and sworn strong enemy living across the sea - combined. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1444147373i/16459412._SY540_.jpg" width="270" height="340" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(The image is by Sandara from Deviant Art)<br><br>I am not kidding: by my estimate the losses of lives here were heavier than in the previous books. To make Tavi's life even less boring he happened to stay exactly on the way of some high-powered ambitious lords to their goals. Can his life get even more exciting than this? It surely can!<br><br>I am happy to say Tavi finally stopped being Gary Stu and became more fleshed out character. So did one other character whose name I skip to avoid spoilers. The end of the book was also quite good; it opened up interesting possibilities for the heroes, especially yet another unnamed person. <br><br>While the parts related to the High Lord and his companions' misadventures are quite boring, Tavi and the First Legion more than make up for this in the excitement department. I look forward to reading the next book of the series and at this point it is probably safe to say that I like it more than the better-known one of the author, The Dresden Files. <br><br>The rating is 4 stars. It is recommended to people who like Dresden Files, but think that Harry Dresden overstayed his welcome, or became annoyed with him. </span>
  <a data-text-id="5295019497458052648" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer8878240634298938108">[4 stars] Academ’s Fury and Cursor’s Fury were two of the best fantasy books I’ve ever read – I loved the snot out of them. They took me on a whirlwind of a ride and so, by comparison, Captain’s Fury was a slower burn, more on par with the first book (although the events that happened within this one still rocked my world).   <span id="freeText8878240634298938108" style="display:none">[4 stars] Academ’s Fury and Cursor’s Fury were two of the best fantasy books I’ve ever read – I loved the snot out of them. They took me on a whirlwind of a ride and so, by comparison, Captain’s Fury was a slower burn, more on par with the first book (although the events that happened within this one still rocked my world). It seemed more like a set up novel for the last couple books in the series and it did a great job generating some momentum. I can’t wait to finish this series – almost everything about it has made me very upset that I didn’t start it ages ago (and that my library holds are taking sooo long to come in). I love it!<br /><br />Via The Obsessive Bookseller at <a href="http://www.nikihawkes.com" rel="nofollow noopener">www.nikihawkes.com</a></span>

<div id="review_955571343" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/955571343" />
    <a title="Kaitlin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin"><img alt="Kaitlin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1481663259p2/19126246.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/955571343?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaitlin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaitlin" href="/user/show/19126246-kaitlin">Kaitlin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9781841497471" href="/book/show/4961946-captain-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19126246-kaitlin?shelf=my-sff-faves">my-sff-faves</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer955571343" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13054583405747990894">To me, this book has been the most fun in the series so far, which is great! I read this as part of the #Rainbowthon and I found myself managing to get through this is just 2 days, very exciting.<br/><br/>This is set in a world where magic is the norm and everyone has at least one weak Fury (kind of a magic spirit). If you are very proficient with the Fury or Furies that you control and use then it's more likely that you're a noble or someone who has a position of power, although some keep the true extent</span>
  <span id="freeText13054583405747990894" style="display:none">To me, this book has been the most fun in the series so far, which is great! I read this as part of the #Rainbowthon and I found myself managing to get through this is just 2 days, very exciting.<br /><br />This is set in a world where magic is the norm and everyone has at least one weak Fury (kind of a magic spirit). If you are very proficient with the Fury or Furies that you control and use then it's more likely that you're a noble or someone who has a position of power, although some keep the true extent of their powers hidden.<br />There are three major races in this book who we follow. The Aleran's are the main race that most of our central character's are from. We then have the Marat race which is largely based on tribes and customs, and have very different ways to the Aleran's. Finally we have the Canim who are a super large wolf-like race. They're often seen as the 'bad-guys' and in this book they're against the Aleran's, but some of them are more reasonable than others.<br /><br />So this story once more follows Tavi as the lead character with others also taking leading roles. Tavi is a young man by the time we meet him in this book and he's been masquerading as Scipio, the young Captain leading troops against the Canim. The war against the Canim has been going on for a while and it's only now that Alera are at full strength and ready to really take them on (and *hopefully* win). Tavi is stuck leading troops and soldiers whilst all around him people are jealous of his position and envious of the men loyal to him. He's in a fair few deadly situations and close calls across the book, but this doesn't stop him from showing us his determination and skilful planning, and resourcefulness when things (inevitably) go wrong.<br /><br />Isana is Tavi's aunt and has basically cared for him from his birth. She's one of the closest people to him, but she's kept a secret about his heritage for a long long time, and she's reluctant to tell Tavi even though he's now old enough. This secret has been the worry of her life, and she's tense and worried about his reaction to it. She's also kind of a pawn in another's game (Lady Aquitine) who wants her to do her bidding in return for earlier help. Overall Isana is also put into some tough predicaments, yet she actually relishes these once they're done with and the unburdening seems to help her expand herself and her powers.<br /><br />Amara is a Curser who is working for the First Lord, Gaius as she has done for much of her life. She's a clever character who knows how to act quickly and do her job well. She's very competent and one of the best wind Fury controllers out there when it comes to flight. She's loyal to Gaius beyond a doubt, and she's happy to accompany him on a very mysterious mission without too much explanation.<br />Despite all this she has a secret which is to do with the man she loves. She's trying to fulfil her role to Gais at all times, but sometimes she wishes things were different and Curser's could get married and live a simple life...<br /><br />Marcus is a member within the troops working with Tavi. He's a man who has a very shady past, but due to some events of the previous books his earlier alliances with the Aquitine's may now be tested and he's not sure who he should root for. He's manipulative and very good at guessing what may come to pass so he's a dangerous character to be on the wrong side of. He also doesn't like to be controlled. His story certainly interested me a lot more as the book went on and we saw him as a more major viewpoint character.<br /><br />Kitai was, once more, my favourite character as she's quick and sharp in all senses of the words. She's funny and can make jokes, but she's also been raised in a way that's very different from the people of Alera because she's a Marat. She's fun to read about and imagine and I feel like she's the sort of person you'd like to be friends with (because being her enemy would be deadly).<br /><br />Finally Gaius himself deserves a fair mention as he's one of the most powerful men in all of the land with many Furies under his command and a long time of ruling and experience. He's a fairly old man by this point of the story but the events of the ongoing conflicts from two sides have forced him to act and take matters into his own hands. At some points of this book his frailty was wonderfully shown and at others his power and immense strength of will and magic was also brilliantly shown. Overall I think he's a bit of a bad-ass :)<br /><br />On the whole this book was just the type of book I was looking for right now. It was fun, fast-paced and a return to character I already knew and enjoyed. Slipping back into the world was very easy and it felt like I could remember everything that I needed to even though it had been a fair time since I last picked up the book before. I thoroughly enjoyed the read through for this and would give it a 5* rating. Recommended as a very fun and fast high fantasy series.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13054583405747990894" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer9591215840607247776">3.5 stars. Another excellent installment in what has turned out to be an above-average epic fantasy series. The description of the book tells enough about the story that I won't re-hash the plot and will simply point out a few things I like about the story. <br/><br/>The progression of Tavi from young, naive, fury-less Country boy to a veteran, capable, fury-full (is that a word) Captain of the Aleran forces has been thoughful, understandable and well done. I also find myself really liking the characters </span>
  <span id="freeText9591215840607247776" style="display:none">3.5 stars. Another excellent installment in what has turned out to be an above-average epic fantasy series. The description of the book tells enough about the story that I won't re-hash the plot and will simply point out a few things I like about the story. <br /><br />The progression of Tavi from young, naive, fury-less Country boy to a veteran, capable, fury-full (is that a word) Captain of the Aleran forces has been thoughful, understandable and well done. I also find myself really liking the characters Butcher has created and believe that he has done a better job in this series at fleshing out the characters and making them three dimensional than in his more popular <i>Dresden</i> books (which I also like by the way). <br /><br />As with the previous books, the political elements are always present and Butcher does a good job in creating tension among the various factions while continuing to introduce new players to the game. I also have enjoyed how Butcher has continuously added new elements to the magical elements of the story in order to keep the story from growing stale, but not does SO MUCH that the story loses its dramatic appeal (the introduction of the "Great Furies" in this book is a good example). <br /><br />Overall, this is top-notch epic fantasy and one I RECOMMEND fans of the genre. Looking forward to the next installment. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9591215840607247776" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362649737" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362649737" />
    <a title="Rob" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10743961-rob"><img alt="Rob" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1422270416p2/10743961.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362649737?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rob" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rob" href="/user/show/10743961-rob">Rob</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=own">own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-2014">read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=read-before-goodreads">read-before-goodreads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10743961-rob?shelf=author-male">author-male</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362649737" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7486115186881725539"><b>Executive Summary:</b> While this one didn't live up to my memory of it, it's still a really fun read with a lot to like.<br/><br/><b>Audio book:</b> At this point, I'm used to Kate Reading as a reader and can't imagine anyone else doing it.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br/>I originally maintained my 5 star rating after finishing my reread, but I think if I'm honest and rate it how I would if I were reading it for the first time, it would be a solid 4 star. This book starts and ends really well, but slows down in the middle some. <br/><br/>Like</span>
  <span id="freeText7486115186881725539" style="display:none"><b>Executive Summary:</b> While this one didn't live up to my memory of it, it's still a really fun read with a lot to like.<br /><br /><b>Audio book:</b> At this point, I'm used to Kate Reading as a reader and can't imagine anyone else doing it.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Full Review</u>
</b><br />I originally maintained my 5 star rating after finishing my reread, but I think if I'm honest and rate it how I would if I were reading it for the first time, it would be a solid 4 star. This book starts and ends really well, but slows down in the middle some. <br /><br />Like the first two books, some of the subplots just move too slow and left me wanting to get back to Tavi's story. In particular Amara's story really dragged for me here. I felt the tedium of her journey a little too much for my liking.<br /><br />The start of this book mostly picks up right where Cursor's Fury leaves off (albeit a few years have passed) with Tavi and the First Aleran fighting the Canim. <br /><br />Mr. Butcher does war well, and I think of all the antagonists of the series, the Canim are by far my favorite. They remind me a bit of Klingons. They really fit the proud warrior trope merged with wolfpack mentality to create a fun and interesting race.<br /><br />The politics are ramped up in this one along with the stakes. Alera is at war on two fronts, and something has to give. The senator and his "bodyguards" remind me of everything I hate about politicians, so Mr. Butcher did a good job on that front I think.<br /><br />The dialogue and the humor are great once again. Mr. Butcher always writes an excellent climax and this one is no different.<br /><br />While there is still a lot yet to resolve, this one ends in a nice place that allowed me to take a short break and read another book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7486115186881725539" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nadine" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nadine" href="/user/show/3759963-nadine">Nadine</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2934558091" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1562941060787612807">I’ll keep this short and spoiler free since Captain’s Fury is the fourth book in the series.<br/><br/>Captain’s Fury is slower than the previous novels, but that does not detract from its awesomeness. If you’ve made it this far into the series, you can forgive it’s slowly pace and lengthy set up for the final two novels.<br/><br/>The series is now embroiled in war. Butcher writes such energetic and gritty war scenes making it easy to follow and visualize. At no point does he glorify war. He shows it in all its dirt</span>
  <span id="freeText1562941060787612807" style="display:none">I’ll keep this short and spoiler free since Captain’s Fury is the fourth book in the series.<br /><br />Captain’s Fury is slower than the previous novels, but that does not detract from its awesomeness. If you’ve made it this far into the series, you can forgive it’s slowly pace and lengthy set up for the final two novels.<br /><br />The series is now embroiled in war. Butcher writes such energetic and gritty war scenes making it easy to follow and visualize. At no point does he glorify war. He shows it in all its dirty details.<br /><br />I especially loved Amara’s journey in this novel. The actual mission she was on and her character’s spiritual, if you will, journey was easily the best aspect of Captain’s Fury. <br /><br />With things concluded as they are, I am very excited to see what’s next for these characters. Princep’s Fury is sure to deliver!<br /></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_39059359" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/39059359" />
    <a title="Reed" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1113585-reed"><img alt="Reed" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343239073p2/1113585.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/39059359?book_show_action=true">Dec 01, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Reed" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Reed" href="/user/show/1113585-reed">Reed</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer39059359" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6470205814498966059">The continuing adventures of Tavi and the rest of the crew. If you are a fan of the series, you know what to expect. The characters get into loads of impossible scrapes, only to somehow pull themselves through.<br/><br/>I've noticed a disturbing trend in this series since the second book--I spend the first quarter to third of the book trying to remember who all the characters are, and where the assorted story lines were going. I spend the next third or so thinking "I love Butcher's novels, but I'm not sur</span>
  <span id="freeText6470205814498966059" style="display:none">The continuing adventures of Tavi and the rest of the crew. If you are a fan of the series, you know what to expect. The characters get into loads of impossible scrapes, only to somehow pull themselves through.<br /><br />I've noticed a disturbing trend in this series since the second book--I spend the first quarter to third of the book trying to remember who all the characters are, and where the assorted story lines were going. I spend the next third or so thinking "I love Butcher's novels, but I'm not sure I'm going to finish this one." I then spend the last third racing through as the action picks up dramatically and I'm eager to read how it finishes.<br /><br />Captain's Fury was much the same. Admittedly, I did remember many of the characters a bit better this time, but I think the series suffers from the large number of recurring characters. Butcher's normally good characterization is noticeably absent here--many of the characters are little more than a name and collection of traits.<br /><br />I did finish, I did enjoy the ending, but I personally think the book has taken some wrong turns along the way. I found the first book refreshing because Tavi was a hero who had to survive through his wits because he had no power of his own. But Butcher has changed this to a typical seemingly weak character who slowly comes into his power. <br /><br />I wish he'd kept Tavi the way he was. A duel Tavi fights near the end of the book perfectly outlines what I mean--the old Tavi would never have been able to do what the current Tavi accomplishes. No swords cutting through metal, superhuman leaps to nearby roofs, etc. <br /><br />I liked Tavi with no access to crafting. He was much more interesting, because he was not like every other fantasy character on the market. I'll probably read the next book, because I read all of Butcher's work. I just hope the next one mixes things up a bit more.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="6470205814498966059" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_381951302" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/381951302" />
    <a title="Kaila" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila"><img alt="Kaila" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525808775p2/3335221.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/381951302?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kaila" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kaila" href="/user/show/3335221-kaila">Kaila</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/7089452-captain-s-fury">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012">fantasy-aficionados-challenge-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3335221-kaila?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer381951302" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5241302935617622007">I am not a Codex Alera fan. So far, the star spread is (links lead to the reviews):<br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219155889' rel='nofollow noopener'>Furies of Calderon (Codex Alera #1)</a> - 2 stars<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251185743' rel='nofollow noopener'>Academ's Fury (Codex Alera #2)</a> - 2 stars<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260944535' rel='nofollow noopener'>Cursor's Fury (Codex Alera #3)</a> - 1 star<br/>And this book, Captain's Fury (Codex Alera #4) - 2 stars<br/><br/>That's not a very good track record to continue on with. And yet, I'm still reading them. Some deep dark part of me obviously wants to know how the story is going to end, and whether any of these characters are ever going to bite it. So </span>
  <span id="freeText5241302935617622007" style="display:none">I am not a Codex Alera fan. So far, the star spread is (links lead to the reviews):<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/219155889" rel="nofollow noopener">Furies of Calderon (Codex Alera #1)</a> - 2 stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/251185743" rel="nofollow noopener">Academ's Fury (Codex Alera #2)</a> - 2 stars<br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260944535" rel="nofollow noopener">Cursor's Fury (Codex Alera #3)</a> - 1 star<br />And this book, Captain's Fury (Codex Alera #4) - 2 stars<br /><br />That's not a very good track record to continue on with. And yet, I'm still reading them. Some deep dark part of me obviously wants to know how the story is going to end, and whether any of these characters are ever going to bite it. So that does say <i>something</i> for this series. It is very readable. It is so...<i>fluffy</i>. Bad things continue to happen but the characters are never in any real danger, because no matter what, something will save them.<br /><br />I love fantasy, there is no way around that. There are of course many reasons why I love fantasy so much, but one reason was actually present in this book. Shock! I know, right? I can't help it, I really like it when characters break down and accept their fate. The readers have known it was coming since the end of book 3 (or longer, depending on how quickly you picked up that the titles basically spoil the entire series), but here, it happens. Tavi accepts who he is, and who his dad was. He will never be without responsibilities again, will never be a little boy in Calderon again. I can't help it; even if I don't like the series, that scene was moving and well done. It was a paradigm shift, and the entire rest of the book plays out around his acceptance. Nothing can ever be the same. This is a big deal!<br /><br />For once, the second half of the book was not taken up by one long, drawn out battle. It is instead a lot more about sneaking around and getting a precise mission completed, rather than throwing legion after legion into battle like all the other books up until this point. A lot of blood still gets shed, of course, but I was getting very tired of half a book of set up just so we could have half a book of battle.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I find just about every character insufferable.<br /><br />The evolution of Finduilas is a side story I've enjoyed, up until now. I love it when bad guys become maybe-almost-kinda good guys. Friendship through adversity and all that. In this particular installment, Finduilas' story, or "Marcus," was just ok. His character was great but some of the...let's say the WAY he got his orders was completely ridiculous. I don't want to spoil anything so I won't go into details, but I feel like the nobility in this series <i>has</i> to have better things to do than harass Tavi out in the middle of nowhere. Apparently, that's the only hobby any of them have. Very frustrating.<br /><br />Amara and Bernard are the worst. I thought their love story stilted from the beginning, while their ludicrous reasons for being married and hiding their marriage is just to create some drama. There was no real reason to write that their marriage had to be hidden, except that for some reason they are considered main characters and must therefore see some face time. Therefore: this marriage must be hidden! Let's talk about how we have to hide our love, endlessly! Plus, their mission in this book is an exercise in ridiculousness. The ONLY reason they are on such a stupid mission is to give them some face time, otherwise Bernard would be up in Calderon doing his count thing. Again, the nobility has nothing better to do than get their own hands dirty and perform their own work. I realize that the nobility houses the strongest furycrafters, but seriously, there's no one else the First Lord could have sent on this absolutely absurd quest? The entire idea behind this subplot was stupid, and then it just keeps on GOING. Walking through the swamp, come to find out, is just not that interesting.<br /><br />The evolution of Tavi has been completely unbelievable to me from the very beginning, but it became a million times worse in, <i>Cursor's Fury</i> (Codex Alera #3). The whole idea of Tavi wresting control of a legion, and then out thinking an entire army, was not only baffling to me, it was also so completely far fetched, I ranted about it for ages over at <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/260944535" rel="nofollow noopener">my review</a> of it. Because of everything that occurred so nonsensically in book 3, book 4 picks up right where it left off, with Tavi having an entire legion so completely loyal they are all willing to do whatever he says at the drop of a hat. Unfortunately, I am still in disbelief to the loyalty, as the whole reason it came around was so preposterous.<br /><br />He then continues to perform death defying acts across the continent, putting himself into one stupid situation after another. I found it all to be worthless - I knew no one would die, no matter how close to death they got, and I knew Tavi would always come up with some crazy scheme, and it would always work out. The whole thing was an exercise in futility for the reader. You know what is going to happen long before it does, so what's the point of reading it? This installation was the most predictable, and I have found EVERY book in this series to be disappointingly predictable. There is no depth here, only fluff.<br /><br />My last note is: I hate the vord. I have hated them since the <i>croach</i> crater in book 1. I'm not even sure why I dislike them so much, but I really really do. Maybe because they're a Borg-style (or Dalek-style) villain but done poorly. Of course, I do feel that both of those villains became caricatures, and were no longer frightening by the end of their respective TV shows. We shall see how I feel after <i>Princeps' Fury</i> (Codex Alera #5), but for some reason I have this feeling I am going to hate that one. Big surprise!<br /><br />Oh, yes! I can't forget to mention how much I hate the word "crow" now. SO MUCH! It's horrible. At least most fantasy books have a few different curse words to choose from. Having only one makes me have eye twitches.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5241302935617622007" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2106250780" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2106250780" />
    <a title="Kostas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas"><img alt="Kostas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1554812738p2/25638423.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2106250780?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kostas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kostas" href="/user/show/25638423-kostas">Kostas</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=epic-high-fantasy">epic-high-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=military-sff">military-sff</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25638423-kostas?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2106250780" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9374082116183086445">7.5/10<br/><br/>Moving towards the second half of the series, where most authors would have already brought their story arcs to their completion, having managed to build a huge world through his imagination, Jim Butcher takes us in <i>Captain’s Fury</i>, the fourth installment, back to the Realm's civil war, into a story of <i>Legionares</i> and Senators, of <i>singulares</i>, pirates and wolfish warriors, and into an adventure of stratagems and conspiracies, of discipline and leadership, and of truth and trust that will test</span>
  <span id="freeText9374082116183086445" style="display:none">7.5/10<br /><br />Moving towards the second half of the series, where most authors would have already brought their story arcs to their completion, having managed to build a huge world through his imagination, Jim Butcher takes us in <i>Captain’s Fury</i>, the fourth installment, back to the Realm's civil war, into a story of <i>Legionares</i> and Senators, of <i>singulares</i>, pirates and wolfish warriors, and into an adventure of stratagems and conspiracies, of discipline and leadership, and of truth and trust that will test the heroes’ abilities more than ever.<br /><br />It’s been two years since the Night of the Red Stars and Lord Kalarus’s rebellion, and the sacrifices they had to make; an instigated war that challenged their very survival, bringing the western regions and the people of Alera into chaos, despair, and disarray, and now, with the Realm being threatened by two fronts, the High Lords and the Senate have at last united their forces under one common purpose - but for Tavi, having stood before the worst possible odds, fighting alongside his <i>legionares</i>, these years were the most difficult he has passed so far.<br />Stationed along with the First Aleran at bridge of the Elinarch, at Tiber River, to repel the Canim forces, Tavi’s young military life has been filled with more responsibilities than ever before, dividing his time among the preparation and the defense of the fortifications, the intense exercise of his growing abilities, and his irresistible lust for Kitai, leaving him barely with any rest.<br />Yet, with the constant conflict between the Canim warriors and their Legions having cost to both too much, as he’ll try to find a peaceful solution that will bring a cessation of hostilities - wanting nothing more than to put an end to the needless bloodshed and waste of lives - when the newly appointed commander of the Senate, the haughty Senator Arnos, in his deep hunger for vengeance, begins his own campaign to wipe them out from their land once and for all, and a political conspiracy sets to undermine anyone that'll stand against it, Tavi and those loyal to him will be faced with the laws of the Realm and a high-risk mission through the seas and prisons of Alera, holding in their hands the fate of all of them.<br /><br />At the second front of the war, at the city of Kalare, Amara, having become the First Lord’s personal liaison, these years she's spent them traveling between the capital and the sieging camps of their Legions, delivering and collecting reports for the course of their forces that has taken her away from Bernard’s company more than she would've liked.<br />But, as her last order will assign her to convene the War Committee at the Elinarch, when the First Lord leads her to the outskirts of the city of Kalare, in a mission of utmost secrecy, she and Bernard will find themselves amidst a dangerous adventure of survival through the forests and the swamps; an adventure that, when the real intentions of their mission are revealed, will bring them into a test that could destroy everything of what they believed in.<br />Meanwhile, Isana, with the secrets of her past having begun to bring her a deep guilt, eating her very soul, when she undertakes to deliver the supplies that she bought with the Dianic League’s funding to the refugees at the Elinarch, she’ll have to take a difficult decision that may well cost her the one person in this world that she loves most; while Valiar Marcus, having taken someone else’s identity these couple years, fighting at the side of a boy - a young man - that he wouldn’t had ever imagined that he would find again, he will have to choose between his loyalty and his honor, and his certain death and the preservation of his life.<br /><br />However, with the war having extended beyond their control, touching the hearts of the slaves and the simple people, when the Canim warriors and their united free forces seem to be ready to surge towards the last defending troops of their Legions, and Lord Kalarus approaches at unleashing a restrained power of vast consequences, Tavi and his companions, Amara and Bernard, and Isana and Araris, will have to find a way to overcome the obstacles that will come before them and put a final end to this war before it’s too late, because if they fail, the future of the Realm of Alera will become more uncertain than ever before.<br /><br />Continuing the threads that he left open in the third book of the series, <i>Cursor’s Fury</i>, and the events that triggered Lord Kalarus’s rebellion and the Canim invasion, Jim Butcher returns once again back to the Realm’s war, immersing us deep into the ranks of the soldiers and the commanding officers between the forces of the Legions and the Canim, showing us the difficulties of the military leadership, the orders and laws that they must follow, and the battles that they must survive, as well as into the lives of the slaves and the simple people of the western regions who, without having the Citizenry’s privilege, falling victims to the manipulation of their seemingly superiors and their political schemes - forcing them to abandon everything they had - brings to light the great impact that have the actions of wrong choices upon them, their homes and their families.<br />But taking to us at the same time and on a journey through the seas, the forests and the swamps of the Realm that brings to the surface a wondrous, unexplored world of creatures and magic, filled with turtle-like Leviathans, enormous Garim lizards and powerful Furies that inhabit beyond the authority of the humans - a world that, showing its good and its bad, reveals its many and different aspects.<br /><br />And, though the book may not be as sweeping as its predecessor, losing its intensity a little in the middle, Butcher manages to bring in <i>Captain’s Fury</i> another exciting novel that blends wonderfully the military fantasy with the political intrigue, traveling us into a story of <i>legionaries</i> and <i>singulares</i>, of Citizens and simple people, of barbarian horsemen and wolfish warriors, but also into an adventure of stratagems and conspiracies, and of trust and truth that, as the characters’ lives get even more complicated, bringing them before greater difficulties, achieves in the end to offer lots of enjoyable moments of thrill and joy, making the anticipation of their next adventures even bigger.<br /><br />All in all, <i>Captain’s Fury</i> is a satisfying fourth book, with Jim Butcher to travels us through the war of the Realm of Alera into an exciting military and political story of <i>Legionares</i>, pirates and <i>singulares</i>, as well as into an adventure of stratagems, conspiracies, and trust that leaves in the end many promises for something even better to come next.<br /><br /><br />Ελληνική κριτική:<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Προχωρώντας προς το δεύτερο μισό της σειράς, εκεί όπου οι περισσότεροι συγγραφείς θα είχαν ήδη φέρει τις ιστορίες στην ολοκλήρωσή τους, έχοντας καταφέρει να χτίσει ένα τεράστιο κόσμο μέσα από την φαντασία του, ο Jim Butcher μας πηγαίνει στο <i>Captain’s Fury</i>, το τέταρτο μέρος, πίσω στον εμφύλιο πόλεμο του Βασιλείου, μέσα σε μια ιστορία <i>Λεγεωνάριων</i> και Γερουσιαστών, <i>σωματοφυλάκων</i>, πειρατών και λυκοειδών πολεμιστών, και σε μια περιπέτεια στρατηγημάτων και συνομωσιών, πειθαρχίας και ηγεσίας, και αλήθειας και εμπιστοσύνης που θα δοκιμάσει τις ικανότητες των ηρώων περισσότερο από ποτέ.<br /><br />Έχουν περάσει δύο χρόνια από την Νύχτα των Κόκκινων Αστεριών και την επανάσταση του Άρχοντα Kalarus, και τις θυσίες που έπρεπε να κάνουν• ένας υποκινούμενος πόλεμος που προκάλεσε την ίδια τους την επιβίωση, φέρνοντας τις δυτικές περιοχές και τους ανθρώπους της Alera μέσα στο χάος, την απελπισία, και την σύγχυση, και τώρα, με το Βασίλειο να απειλείται από δύο μέτωπα, οι Υψηλοί Άρχοντες και η Σύγκλητος έχουν επιτέλους ενώσει τις δυνάμεις τους κάτω από έναν κοινό σκοπό - αλλά για τον Tavi, έχοντας σταθεί ενώπιον των χειρότερων δυνατών πιθανοτήτων, πολεμώντας στο πλευρό των <i>λεγεωνάριών</i> του, αυτά τα χρόνια ήταν τα πιο δύσκολα που έχει περάσει μέχρι τώρα.<br />Σταθμευμένος μαζί με την Πρώτη Αλέρια στην γέφυρα του Elinarch, στον Ποταμό Tiber, για να απωθήσουν τις δυνάμεις των Canim, η νεαρή στρατιωτική ζωή του Tavi έχει γεμίσει με περισσότερες ευθύνες από ποτέ, μοιράζοντας τον χρόνο του ανάμεσα στην ετοιμασία και την άμυνα των οχυρωμάτων, στην έντονη εξάσκηση των αυξανόμενων ικανοτήτων του, και τον ακαταμάχητο πόθο του για την Kitai, αφήνοντάς τον με τα βίας με οποιαδήποτε ξεκούραση.<br />Κι όμως, με την συνεχής αντιμαχία μεταξύ των Canim πολεμιστών και της Λεγεώνας τους να έχει κοστίσει και στους δύο πάρα πολλά, καθώς θα επιχειρήσει να βρει μια ειρηνική λύση που θα φέρει μια παύση των εχθροπραξιών - θέλοντας όσο τίποτε άλλο παρά να βάλει ένα τέλος στην άσκοπη αιματοχυσία και σπατάλη ζωών - όταν ο νεοδιορισμένος διοικητής της Συγκλήτου, ο υπεροπτικός Γερουσιαστής Arnos, στην βαθιά πείνα του για εκδίκηση, ξεκινήσει την δικιά του εκστρατεία για να τους εξαλείψει από την χώρα τους μια και καλή, και μια πολιτική συνομωσία θέσει να υπονομεύσει οποιονδήποτε που θα σταθεί ενάντιά της, ο Tavi και αυτοί που είναι αφοσιωμένοι σε αυτόν θα βρεθούν αντιμέτωποι τους νόμους του Βασιλείου και μια υψηλού κινδύνου αποστολή μέσα από τις θάλασσες και τις φυλακές της Alera, κρατώντας στα χέρια τους την μοίρα όλων τους.<br /><br />Στο δεύτερο μέτωπο του πολέμου, στην πόλη του Kalare, η Amara, έχοντας γίνει η προσωπική σύνδεσμος του Πρώτου Άρχοντα, αυτά τα χρόνια τα έχει περάσει ταξιδεύοντας μεταξύ της πρωτεύουσας και των πολιορκητικών στρατοπέδων των Λεγεώνων τους, παραδίδοντας και συλλέγοντας αναφορές για την πορεία των δυνάμεών τους που την έχει πάρει μακριά από την συντροφιά του Bernard περισσότερο απ’ όσο θα ήθελε.<br />Όμως, καθώς η τελευταία της διαταγή θα της αναθέσει να συγκαλέσει την Επιτροπή Πολέμου στο Elinarch, όταν ο Πρώτος Άρχοντας την οδηγήσει στα περίχωρα της πόλης του Kalare, σε μια αποστολή ύψιστης μυστικότητας, αυτή και ο Bernard θα βρεθούν εν μέσω μιας επικίνδυνης περιπέτειας επιβίωσης μέσα από τα δάση και τους βάλτους• μια περιπέτεια που, όταν οι πραγματικές προθέσεις της αποστολής τους αποκαλυφθούν, θα τους φέρει μέσα σε μια δοκιμή που θα μπορούσε να διαλύσει όλα σε όσα πίστευαν.<br />Εν τω μεταξύ, η Isana, με τα μυστικά του παρελθόντος της να έχουν αρχίσει να της φέρνουν μια βαθιά ενοχή, τρώγοντας την ίδια της την ψυχή, όταν αναλάβει να παραδώσει τις προμήθειες που αγόρασε με την χρηματοδότηση της Ντιανικής Συμμαχίας στους πρόσφυγες στο Elinarch, θα πρέπει να πάρει μια δύσκολη που μπορεί κάλλιστα να της κοστίσει το μοναδικό άτομο στον κόσμο αυτό που αγαπάει περισσότερο• ενώ ο Valiar Marcus, έχοντας πάρει την ταυτότητα κάποιου αλλουνού αυτά τα δύο χρόνια, πολεμώντας στο πλευρό ενός αγοριού - ενός νεαρού άντρα - που δεν θα είχε φανταστεί ποτέ του ότι θα έβρισκε ξανά, θα πρέπει να επιλέξει μεταξύ της αφοσίωσης του και τιμής του, και του σίγουρου θανάτου του και της διατήρησης της ζωής του.<br /><br />Ωστόσο, με τον πόλεμο να έχει επεκταθεί πέρα από τον έλεγχό τους, αγγίζοντας τις καρδιές των σκλάβων και των απλών ανθρώπων, όταν οι Canim πολεμιστές και οι ενωμένες ελεύθερες δυνάμεις τους φανούν να είναι έτοιμοι να ξεχυθούν προς τα τελευταία αμυνόμενα στρατεύματα των Λεγεώνων τους, και ο Άρχοντας Kalarus πλησιάσει στο να ελευθερώσει μια συγκρατημένη δύναμη απέραντων συνεπειών, ο Tavi και οι σύντροφοί του, η Amara και ο Bernard, και η Isana και o Araris, θα πρέπει να βρουν ένα τρόπο για να ξεπεράσουν τα εμπόδια που θα έρθουν ενώπιόν τους και να βάλουν ένα οριστικό τέλος σε αυτόν τον πόλεμο πριν να είναι πολύ αργά, γιατί αν αποτύχουν, το μέλλον του Βασιλείου της Alera θα γίνει πιο αβέβαιο από ποτέ.<br /><br />Συνεχίζοντας τα νήματα που άφησε ανοιχτά στο τρίτο βιβλίο της σειράς, το <i>Cursor’s Fury</i>, και τα γεγονότα που έδωσαν το έναυσμα της επανάσταση του Άρχοντα Kalarus και της εισβολής των Canim, ο Jim Butcher επιστρέφει για ακόμη μια φορά πίσω στον πόλεμο το Βασιλείου, βυθίζοντάς μας βαθιά μέσα στις τάξεις των στρατιωτών και των διοικητών μεταξύ των δυνάμεων της Alera και των Canim, δείχνοντάς μας τις δυσκολίες της στρατιωτικής ηγεσίας, των διαταγών και των νόμων που πρέπει να ακολουθήσουν, και τις μάχες που πρέπει να επιβιώσουν, όπως επίσης και μέσα στις ζωές των σκλάβων και των απλών ανθρώπων των δυτικών περιοχών οι οποίοι, χωρίς να έχουν το προνόμιο των Πολιτών, πέφτοντας θύματα στην χειραγώγηση των φαινομενικά ανώτερών τους και των πολιτικών σκευωριών τους - αναγκάζοντάς τους να εγκαταλείψουν ότι είχαν - φέρνει στο φως την μεγάλη επίπτωση που έχουν οι πράξεις των λάθων επιλογών πάνω σε αυτούς, τα σπίτια και τις οικογένειές τους.<br />Αλλά πηγαίνοντάς μας ταυτόχρονα και μέσα σε ένα ταξίδι μέσα από τις θάλασσες, τα δάση και τους βάλτους του Βασιλείου που φέρνει στην επιφάνεια έναν θαυμαστό, ανεξερεύνητο κόσμο πλασμάτων και μαγείας, γεμάτο με χελωνοειδή Λεβιάθαν, τεράστιες Garim σαύρες και πανίσχυρες Ερινύες που κατοικούν πέρα από την εξουσία των ανθρώπων - ένας κόσμος που, δείχνοντας τα καλά και τα κακά του, αποκαλύπτει τις πολλές και διαφορετικές πτυχές του.<br /><br />Και, παρ' όλο που το βιβλίο μπορεί να μην είναι τόσο σαρωτικό όσο ο προκάτοχός του, χάνοντας την έντασή του λίγο στην μέση, ο Butcher καταφέρνει να φέρει στο <i>Captain’s Fury</i> ένα ακόμη συναρπαστικό μυθιστόρημα που αναμιγνύει υπέροχα την στρατιωτική φαντασία με την πολιτική ίντριγκα, ταξιδεύοντάς μας μέσα σε μια ιστορία <i>λεγεωνάριων</i> και <i>σωματοφυλάκων</i>, Πολιτών και απλών ανθρώπων, βάρβαρων καβαλάρηδων και λυκοειδών πολεμιστών, αλλά και σε μια περιπέτεια στρατηγημάτων και συνομωσιών, και εμπιστοσύνης και αλήθειας που, καθώς οι ζωές των χαρακτήρων περιπλέκονται ακόμη περισσότερο, φέρνοντάς τους ενώπιον μεγαλύτερων δυσκολιών, επιτυγχάνει στο τέλος να προσφέρει μπόλικες απολαυστικές στιγμές συγκίνησης και χαράς, κάνοντας την αναμονή των επόμενων περιπετειών τους ακόμη πιο μεγάλη. <br /><br />Όλα για όλα, το <i>Captain’s Fury</i> είναι ικανοποιητικό τέταρτο βιβλίο, με τον Jim Butcher να μας ταξιδεύει μέσα από τον πόλεμο του Βασιλείου της Alera μέσα σε μια ακόμη συναρπαστική στρατιωτική και πολιτική ιστορία <i>Λεγεωνάριων</i>, πειρατών και <i>σωματοφυλάκων</i>, όπως επίσης και σε μια περιπέτεια στρατηγημάτων, συνομωσιών και εμπιστοσύνης που αφήνει στο τέλος πολλές υποσχέσεις για κάτι ακόμη καλύτερο να έρθει στην συνέχεια. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

  <span id="freeText1842951659073958045" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379797315i/630051._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So I think I've figured Butcher's style :) And yeah, looks like we do jump two years for each consecutive books. Dunno if I like that in terms of story wise. <br><br>So Octavian and Kitai sound like they've FINALLY done the deed. Kitai FINALLY has her horse. Tavi is still Captain. And the Cane are still roaming, now with ex-slave recruits! No doubt Tavi will win the Aleran folks back to his side. AANNDD sounds like Tavi may just be boinking his Cousin or Step Sister! *Shudders* Eww! (Butcher keeps banging on about Kitai and her eyes being like Tavi's) Explains Gaius and his comment. Nice to see the Marat scouts have arrived. And they aren't ashamed of being nude (Love that scene! So funny) Yip, I am mad folks kept his true lineage a secret. Dangerous times. And, looks like he truly has come into his furies! <br><br>Holy non predictable batman! Amara didn't fly in to see Bernard like she always does at the beginning of a novel! It sounds as though her speed may come into play later. I am curious about Isana/Araris are they or aren't they? Sounds like they aren't since Araris is back with Tavi as his body guard. Still not sure what Gaius wants from Fidelas or what Fidelas wants. He's prime to strike down Tavi as his adviser but he hasn't. <br><br>Hhmm, Lady Aquitaine has Fidelas firmly secured to kill Octavian. Bet he doesn't since he seems to now think Tavi will make a good first lord. Once again, foolish egotistical old men who haven't set foot on a battle field are playing games with legionnaires who have. Once again, they aren't listening to what the REAL threat the Cane is.<br><br>I wonder WHY Gaius doesn't out Octavian now. He's slowly pushing him out front to get folks loyal and used to him BEING the Princeps, but he still doesn't out right say he is. He's in more danger if he's unaware WHY folks are suddenly after him. <br><br>Bad ass! Gaius is FINALLY going to join the war! I'm hoping we have an actual epic battle between he and Kalare. Looking forward to it. *Chuckles* Figures he'd drag Bernard/Amara into his little crew :)<br><br>Damn it Isana! leaving it up to Araris to tell Tavi about his lineage. Coward. I understand, but fucking frustrating. Likewise Tavi's reaction. Araris had it right. He should've talked to Isana before leaving. Loved Araris saluting Tavi as the Princeps he is. Quick of Tavi to run through ALL the implications though. Smart guy. <br><br>Oh, also got a look into WHY Gaius had Tavi bunk with Max which had me suspicious, but it was only tactical. And political. Clever man. Now, I need answers to the whole Kitai thing. No doubt Tavi will return from battle and with valor not doubt LOL Wonder if this will change the possible meeting between Tavi/Nasag. <br><br>Arnos the dumb shit! Upstaged by Octavian so he has to resort to a order he damn well knows Tavi will break! No doubt he'll maneuver his way around. But still. Murdering all those poor people :(<br><br>Ah ha! I think I have it. Gaius has a "Minor" infection at present. With their mission to save Kalare civilians from a "Great Fury" (FIRE MOUNTAIN) and a mass funeral pyre, Gaius NEEDS to stop it. So, I have a feeling Gaius will fall to this infection and Amara will have to dash and bring a watercrafter to save the First Lord. <br><br>Woot they told Cyril! Tavi is the Princeps! Nicely played of him. Arnos is gonna rue the day he opposed Tavi. Max and the others coming to his aid upon return was cool. Shows just how influential Tavi is. Initially thought Gaius would be taken to the legion where Tavi was and bail him, but no. Did it on his own :) Natch. <br><br>Nice of Tavi to be kind and understanding toward Isana. Awesome that they're gonna talk later :) Bloody Crows they're gonna sneak Varg out of the gray tower AFTER Tavi himself made changes to security years ago? Should be interesting indeed LOL <br><br>WAHOO! Isana got some balls! Impressive run through the leviathan :) What was with her power surging like that? Maybe it's like Tavi? and her FULL powers took time to manifest. Maybe the vast expanse of the ocean? maybe Tavi believing in her? Maybe cause she's unburdened now? <br><br>Araris bested by a female? Now THIS should be good. Wonder if Alderick has any luck with the woman. Like that he incorporated the move the woman used on Rari was incorporated into Tavi's training. Good of him to allow Tavi to ask about Septimus :) <br><br>While I like Isana/Kitai bonding, just seems a little too convenient that they get along famously. Like Kitai taking the Mickey out of Isana though :) So Rari thinks Septimus may have passed on his furies to Isana. Why'd no one pass Tavi any? <br><br>Cross fingers Bernard isn't TOTALLY blind. Damn Gaius is bad ass! He could have saved MILLIONS! being on the field from day 1. Aww how sweet Araris proposed! during a kidnap no less LOL FINALLY Tavi has come out as the Princeps. Why the heck call Arnos to Jurus Macto!<br><br>Was the shaking and red light the Kalare mountain waking? Gaius? Hard to believe it's Tavi, unless him claiming his name had something to do with it? Varg and Nasag are father son? Interesting! Loved that.<br><br>LOVED the fight. Had no doubts Tavi would come through. Good advice from Rari as well. I still don't believe Fidelias will stake Tavi. HOPEFULLY, he uses it on Lady Aquataine. Good of Isana to help out as a medic while she waited :) <br><br>I know what pisses Amara off most is that Gaius LIED about the possibilities at Kalare? but he's right. Had he let Kalare release the fury, he would have taken MANY more with him by trapping them in town. It was a lose, lose situation. I am HIGHLY disappointed we didn't see a Gaius/Kalare showdown. I doubt Kalare is dead. LOVED His and Tavi's "Grandfather/Son" interaction at the end. <br><br>Arnos getting slapped by Octavian was petty. It's like striking a dog. Unnecessary. The man is all but dead. No need to assert your authority by striking a dead man. Pathetic. And about the only time I've been disappointed in hi other than getting flowers for the girl in book 1. <br><br>Meh, KNEW Lady Aquataine wasn't dead. Take a lot more than that to kill the bitch. Hopefully, Fidelas makes it. Or not. Don't care each wise. Am curious about Lord Aquataine. KNEW the Vord was in the Cane island. But what, 4 years will probably pass if Butcher holds true. In that time I expect them to have spread to far and wide. 2 years is WAY to long for me as it is.<br><br>Isana wanting to go after the folks who hurt Septimus and may hurt Tavi was bad ass. I'm with Rari though. Her anger will lead to recklessness, which leads to death. Best leave well enough alone until the right moment :) and I do hope she gets her vengeance. Sounds like Kalare was the one who orchestrated the Septimus kill. To bad she and Rari will have to wait to marry :(<br><br>Unlike Bernard and Amara! they're off to play the happy house hold at last :) Happy for em. Hopefully, they can settle and have their young now :) No doubt these two get dragged into the drama again. Have a feeling Amara may forgive but not forget Gaius. Speaking of . . Sounds as though he's ill. I hope not, as I notice the title of the last book *Shuddders* I'm hoping it's just Gaius passing on the mantle to the next generation. <br><br>Over all? My favorite one yet :) Butcher seems to be reading my reviews LOL (Joking) since he has added small little differences here and there that I appreciated. </span>

<div id="review_2475730576" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=2018">2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=action-adventure-mystery-suspense">action-adventure-mystery-suspense</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=part-of-a-series">part-of-a-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=stars-3-5">stars-3-5</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=military">military</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=borrowed-library">borrowed-library</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39942856-jennifer?shelf=safe">safe</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2475730576" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1220203463621829367">3.5 stars. The perfect combination of action, intrigue, relationship and character development, I enjoyed this one the most of the series so far. The different story lines, settings, and points of view helped to move the overall plot along quite nicely. The H was really my favourite character. Unfortunately, Isana turned into a bit of a caricature in this one, but then again I've never really liked her. Looking forward to book five!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1298923672" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1298923672" />
    <a title="Tosh" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/43670791-tosh"><img alt="Tosh" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1515175943p2/43670791.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1298923672?book_show_action=true">Jun 04, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tosh" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tosh" href="/user/show/43670791-tosh">Tosh</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/43670791-tosh?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1298923672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10473568137868726201">Tavi has grown so much within these 4 books, discovering some very important things about himself. Most of what he learns has in one way or another been hinted at in previous books, so I don’t really think the discoveries came as much of a surprise. Anticipating when these things would be revealed was still exciting though.<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>Enemies are far more faithful than friends…more dependable than allies.</i>
</blockquote> <br/><br/>Tavi’s interactions with Varg and Nasaug are some of my most favorite moments. Over the course of t</span>
  <span id="freeText10473568137868726201" style="display:none">Tavi has grown so much within these 4 books, discovering some very important things about himself. Most of what he learns has in one way or another been hinted at in previous books, so I don’t really think the discoveries came as much of a surprise. Anticipating when these things would be revealed was still exciting though.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>Enemies are far more faithful than friends…more dependable than allies.</i>
</blockquote> <br /><br />Tavi’s interactions with Varg and Nasaug are some of my most favorite moments. Over the course of time Tavi has gained an understanding of their social structure and has learned to use it to his advantage, also earning their deep respect, but not necessarily revoking his status as an enemy. It’s a very thin line he walks, which makes it all the more awesome. He’s created a very tentative relationship with the Canim, and I’m curious to see how long that lasts, and how far that will extend to the rest of Alera.<br /><br />And of course, the First Lord is still battling the ongoing political scheming within his borders. It remains to be seen how the rest of Alera will feel with his most recent decision, and if/how his political enemies will use this event to further their causes. <br /><br />Creatures are stilling threatening the security of the realm, High Lords are still maneuvering for power, and more secrets are coming to light, so I’m looking forward to the next two books.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10473568137868726201" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('pBgYV5oA6T+rmD+t/drC0te6VjyoUoeN0X18U9HOqpoOzjEfBYRdmbcPHd5/c6ZINdqCZj7ieVqDJ+TpfbQEEA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Imvag01RTUXARn+hKXDP0vGnF0CiXrfwpRkNkz5P40OIvfPL0tX549zRXdKr2atIE8fDGjTuSSf3Q5UpkjVNyQ==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer4920913929593492942">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly.   <span id="freeText4920913929593492942" style="display:none">Jim Butcher is the author of the Dresden Files, the Codex Alera, and a new steampunk series, the Cinder Spires. His resume includes a laundry list of skills which were useful a couple of centuries ago, and he plays guitar quite badly. An avid gamer, he plays tabletop games in varying systems, a variety of video games on PC and console, and LARPs whenever he can make time for it. Jim currently resides mostly inside his own head, but his head can generally be found in his home town of Independence, Missouri.<br /><br />Jim goes by the moniker Longshot in a number of online locales. He came by this name in the early 1990′s when he decided he would become a published author. Usually only 3 in 1000 who make such an attempt actually manage to become published; of those, only 1 in 10 make enough money to call it a living. The sale of a second series was the breakthrough that let him beat the long odds against attaining a career as a novelist.<br /><br />All the same, he refuses to change his nickname.<br /></span>
